### Assistant
> Yes. What you have is enough to build an **envelopes ingestion pattern** and populate `envelopes` + (optionally) `packets`/`packet_items` if you want each envelope to auto-create a packet.
> 
> Right now your `envelopes` table is missing a few fields you *clearly need* (envelope number, case number, court location, judge, status timestamps). You can still store everything in `notes` as JSON, but you’ll regret it later. So I’m going to give you:
> 
> 1) **What to change in the `envelopes` table** (minimal add-ons)  
> 2) **How to represent each envelope** in your schema  
> 3) A **Gemini prompt** that outputs import-ready CSVs for:
>    - `envelopes.csv`
>    - `packets.csv`
>    - `packet_items.csv` (optional)
> 4) A **worked example** of Envelope #37268798 using your data
> 
> ---
> 
> # 1) Minimal envelope table upgrades (recommended)
> Your current `envelopes` table:
> 
> - has `confirmation_number`, but that sounds like “receipt number”, not the **Envelope #**
> - has `court_system`, but you need court location + judge
> - doesn’t capture case number
> - doesn’t capture accepted/rejected timestamp
> - doesn’t capture service mode summary
> 
> ### Add these columns (minimal, high value)
> 
> ```sql
> alter table public.envelopes
> add column if not exists envelope_number text,         -- "37268798"
> add column if not exists case_number text,             -- "49D03-2501-MF-002559"
> add column if not exists court_location text,          -- "Marion Superior Court 3"
> add column if not exists judge_name text,              -- "Miller, Gary L"
> add column if not exists submitted_by text,            -- "CODY RICE-VELASQUEZ"
> add column if not exists submitted_username text,      -- "crice4485@gmail.com"
> add column if not exists review_at timestamptz,        -- "12/11/2025 8:33 AM"
> add column if not exists filing_status text;           -- Accepted/Rejected etc.
> ```
> 
> Keep `confirmation_number` for whatever eFile gives you (sometimes separate from envelope #).
> 
> If you don’t want to alter schema today, you can shove these into `notes` JSON, but schema is cleaner.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 2) How to model envelope contents with what you already have
> 
> ## A) Envelope = transport container
> One row in `envelopes` per envelope submission.
> 
> ## B) Packet = logical grouping of documents inside that envelope
> One row in `packets` per envelope **(packet_type = 'efile')**, linked to the phase.
> 
> ## C) Packet items = each filing document in that envelope
> Each lead doc becomes a `packet_item` referencing `documents` (once those PDFs exist in `documents`).
> 
> ### Practical ingestion approach
> - Create `envelopes` rows first.
> - Create `packets` rows next (one per envelope).
> - Create placeholder `packet_items` rows with `sort_order` only, and store `lookup_filename` in `notes` or metadata until the `documents` rows exist.
> - Once `documents` is populated, backfill packet_items.document_id by matching `storage_path` or `file_path`.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 3) Workstream + phase mapping for these
> All of these envelopes are court filing related → Phase **01** (court record).  
> Workstream: `court_record`
> 
> So:
> - `phase_id = '01'`
> - `workstream = 'court_record'`
> - `court_system = 'IN_eFile'` (or whatever you standardize)
> 
> ---
> 
> # 4) CSV target format (so you can import cleanly)
> 
> ## envelopes.csv (recommended columns)
> If you add the suggested columns, use:
> 
> - id (blank)
> - user_id (blank)
> - recipient_email (blank unless served party email)
> - recipient_name (blank)
> - status (submitted/accepted/rejected)  ← your schema’s allowed values are weird; see note below
> - sent_at (use submitted datetime)
> - created_at (blank)
> - updated_at (blank)
> - phase_id (01)
> - court_system (e.g., IN_eFile)
> - confirmation_number (use transaction id or confirmation number if distinct)
> - rejection_reason (blank)
> - notes (JSON string containing all raw details)
> - envelope_number
> - case_number
> - court_location
> - judge_name
> - submitted_by
> - submitted_username
> - review_at
> - filing_status
> 
> ### Your `envelopes.status` CHECK is currently:
> `draft/submitted/accepted/rejected` (fine)  
> But default says `prepared` in your earlier schema; ignore that—use allowed values.
> 
> ---
>

> - name: `EFILE Envelope 37268798 — Motions/Proposed Orders/Exhibits`
> - packet_type: `efile`

> # 6) Gemini prompt to convert your pasted envelope text into CSVs
> Use this prompt. It will output **envelopes.csv** plus optional packet CSVs.
> 
> ```text
> You are a court e-filing data normalizer.
> 
> Input: raw envelope detail text pasted from the eFile portal.
> 
> Task: Convert the envelope(s) into import-ready CSV rows for Supabase.
> 
> Tables:
> - envelopes
> - packets (optional: one packet per envelope, packet_type='efile')
> - packet_items (optional: one per lead document, use lookup_filename in notes JSON because document_id is unknown)
> 
> Rules:
> 1) Produce envelopes.csv with one row per envelope.
>    - Use status: accepted/rejected/submitted
>    - Put all non-modeled fields into notes as JSON (stringified).
>    - phase_id='01'
>    - court_system='IN_eFile'
>    - envelope_number is the "Envelope #" value
>    - case_number is "Case #"
> 
> 2) If generating packets:
>    - packets.csv: one row per envelope, packet_type='efile', phase_id='01'
>    - packet_items.csv: one row per lead document with sort_order
>    - packet_id should be a placeholder like "PACKET_ENVELOPE_37268798" to be replaced later.
> 
> 3) Dates:
>    - Normalize to ISO 8601 (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS+00)
>    - If timezone unknown, output without offset.
> 
> Output:
> - envelopes.csv in a code block
> - packets.csv in a code block (if produced)
> - packet_items.csv in a code block (if produced)
> 
> Begin with the envelope text below and extract ALL envelopes present.
> ```

> # 7) Two fast fixes you should do before importing anything else
> ### Fix 1: Envelope status enum mismatch risk
> Your envelope `status` check currently includes: `draft/submitted/accepted/rejected`. Good.
> 
> But your earlier “default prepared” conflicts. Ensure the live check constraint matches allowed values. You already know how to verify constraints.
> 
> ### Fix 2: Create a stable “envelope_number unique per user”
> Add this to prevent duplicate imports:
> 
> ```sql
> alter table public.envelopes
> add constraint envelopes_user_envelope_number_unique
> unique (user_id, envelope_number);
> ```

### User
> alter

### Assistant
> Perfect. Altering is the right move. Here’s the exact build-out so your `envelopes` table can represent what eFile actually gives you, without stuffing everything into `notes`.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1) SQL: Alter `public.envelopes` (add the fields you need)
> 
> Run this in Supabase SQL editor:
> 
> ```sql
> alter table public.envelopes
>   add column if not exists envelope_number text,
>   add column if not exists case_number text,
>   add column if not exists court_location text,
>   add column if not exists judge_name text,
>   add column if not exists submitted_by text,
>   add column if not exists submitted_username text,
>   add column if not exists review_at timestamptz,
>   add column if not exists filing_status text;
> ```
> 
> ### Add uniqueness so you can re-import safely
> ```sql
> alter table public.envelopes
>   add constraint if not exists envelopes_user_envelope_number_unique
>   unique (user_id, envelope_number);
> ```
> 
> ### Add indexes you will use immediately
> ```sql
> create index if not exists envelopes_case_number_idx on public.envelopes (case_number);
> create index if not exists envelopes_phase_idx on public.envelopes (phase_id);
> create index if not exists envelopes_status_idx on public.envelopes (status);
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2) Optional but strongly recommended: normalize casing (so imports don’t break)
> Your `envelopes.status` is constrained. If you ever import `Accepted` instead of `accepted`, you’ll trip again.
> 
> ```sql
> create or replace function public.normalize_envelope_fields()
> returns trigger
> language plpgsql
> as $$
> begin
>   if new.status is not null then new.status := lower(new.status); end if;
>   if new.filing_status is not null then new.filing_status := lower(new.filing_status); end if;
>   return new;
> end;
> $$;
> 
> drop trigger if exists trg_normalize_envelope_fields on public.envelopes;
> 
> create trigger trg_normalize_envelope_fields
> before insert or update on public.envelopes
> for each row
> execute function public.normalize_envelope_fields();
> ```

### Assistant
> Two separate issues, both fixable fast.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 1) SQL error: `ADD CONSTRAINT IF NOT EXISTS` is not valid Postgres syntax
> 
> Postgres supports `IF NOT EXISTS` for **indexes**, not for **constraints**. That’s why you got:
> 
> > syntax error at or near "not"
> 
> ### Use this instead (safe + idempotent)
> Run:
> 
> ```sql
> do $$
> begin
>   if not exists (
>     select 1
>     from pg_constraint
>     where conname = 'envelopes_user_envelope_number_unique'
>   ) then
>     alter table public.envelopes
>       add constraint envelopes_user_envelope_number_unique
>       unique (user_id, envelope_number);
>   end if;
> end $$;
> ```
> 
> If you don’t care about idempotent, simplest is:
> 
> ```sql
> alter table public.envelopes
>   add constraint envelopes_user_envelope_number_unique
>   unique (user_id, envelope_number);
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 2) CSV import error: your “CSV” isn’t a clean CSV for the importer
> 
> The Supabase importer is treating your first row as headers because:
> - either you didn’t include a header row at all, or
> - your header row got mangled
> - and **your JSON includes commas/quotes**, which breaks spreadsheet parsing if not escaped perfectly
> 
> That’s why it thinks columns are named:
> `"37268798"`, `"49D03-2501..."`, etc.
>

### Assistant
> You’re importing via **CSV**, and CSV imports do **not** execute your column default `DEFAULT auth.uid()` the way an authenticated insert does. So `user_id` comes in as **NULL**, and the NOT NULL constraint blows up.
> 
> That’s exactly what the failing row shows: `user_id = null`.
> 
> You have three viable fixes. Pick the one that matches how you’re loading data.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Fix Option A (best): import with SQL, not CSV
> If you run inserts in the SQL editor while logged in, `auth.uid()` will populate automatically **if you omit user_id**, but only if the SQL runs under an auth context. In Supabase SQL editor it often runs as service/admin context where `auth.uid()` is null, so this is inconsistent.
> 
> So: **don’t rely on auth.uid() for backfills**.
> 
> ---
>

### User
> im the only user can we default it on all tables and also theres what 20 tables and gemini is not populating them correctly. what can we do.

### Assistant
> You can force this to stop being fragile, but you need to choose the right lever. Right now you’re fighting two problems:
> 
> 1) **CSV import runs “unauthenticated”**, so `auth.uid()` defaults don’t fire reliably.  
> 2) Gemini is **not a deterministic ETL tool**; it will keep producing inconsistent enums/headers/joins unless you lock it down.
> 
> If you’re the only user, you have two sane paths.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Path 1 (recommended): Keep `user_id`, but auto-fill it at the database layer
> This preserves security and future-proofs you, but removes the pain.
> 
> ## A) Create a constant “owner” setting in Postgres
> Pick your user UUID (you already have it):  
> `e7b2ecff-2e1b-4b96-9627-36f069519521`
> 
> Run:
> 
> ```sql
> create schema if not exists app;
> 
> create or replace function app.owner_id()
> returns uuid
> language sql
> stable
> as $$
>   select 'e7b2ecff-2e1b-4b96-9627-36f069519521'::uuid
> $$;
> ```
> 
> ## B) Add a trigger that fills `user_id` when NULL (for every table)
> Example for `envelopes`:
> 
> ```sql
> create or replace function app.fill_user_id()
> returns trigger
> language plpgsql
> as $$
> begin
>   if new.user_id is null then
>     new.user_id := app.owner_id();
>   end if;
>   return new;
> end;
> $$;
> 
> drop trigger if exists trg_fill_user_id_envelopes on public.envelopes;
> 
> create trigger trg_fill_user_id_envelopes
> before insert on public.envelopes
> for each row
> execute function app.fill_user_id();
> ```
> 
> ### Apply to all tables with user_id
> You have ~20 tables. You can copy/paste the trigger block and change the table/trigger name. This is the quickest “make imports work” fix without destroying your schema.
> 
> **Important:** This works for CSV imports because triggers execute server-side.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Path 2 (fastest, but sloppy): Remove `user_id` entirely
> If you truly will never have multiple users, you can drop `user_id` columns and simplify. I don’t recommend it because:
> - You already built RLS patterns
> - You will regret it if you ever want to share read-only access with counsel/support
> - It’s painful to re-add later
> 
> If you still want this path, say so and I’ll give you the drop script.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The real issue: Gemini is not populating 20 tables correctly
> You need to stop asking Gemini to “populate all tables” directly.
> 
> ## What to do instead: deterministic two-stage ETL
> ### Stage 1: Gemini produces ONE canonical intermediate file
> Gemini should output **only** these normalized “staging tables” as CSV/JSON:
> 
> 1) `stg_actors`
> 2) `stg_documents`
> 3) `stg_violations`
> 4) `stg_harms`
> 5) `stg_damage_entries`
> 6) `stg_credit_events`
> 7) `stg_links` (generic relationships: violation↔doc, harm↔doc, harm↔violation, violation↔authority)
> 
> That’s it.
> 
> ### Stage 2: Postgres functions ingest staging → real tables
> You then run SQL that:
> - upserts actors
> - upserts documents
> - upserts violations/harms/etc.
> - resolves joins by `code`/`path` rather than UUIDs
> - enforces enums and lowercasing
> - prevents duplicates with unique constraints
> 
> This is how you make the system **repeatable** and immune to “Gemini creativity.”
> 
> ---
> 
> # Minimum viable fix you can implement today (no new app code)
> ## Step 1 — Add `fill_user_id()` trigger to every table with user_id
> That stops the NOT NULL failures.
> 
> ## Step 2 — Add uniqueness constraints so re-imports don’t duplicate
> Examples:
> - actors: `unique(user_id, code)`
> - documents: `unique(user_id, storage_path)` (or file_path)
> - violations: `unique(user_id, violation_code)`
> - harms: `unique(user_id, harm_code)` (or title+date if you don’t have codes)
> - join tables: unique composite keys (violation_id, document_id), etc.
> 
> ## Step 3 — Force normalization triggers
> - lower(actor_type)
> - lower(status fields)
> - lower(violation_type, severity, bureau, dispute_status)
> 
> This prevents 90% of import failures.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The tool that will actually fix “Gemini isn’t populating correctly”
> Give Gemini a STRICT contract: one output only (staging) + strict enums.
> 
> Here is the prompt you should use going forward (copy/paste):
> 
> ```text
> You are an ETL generator. You will NOT populate the final database tables.
> 
> Output ONLY the following CSV files, with EXACT headers, and STRICT enum compliance:
> 
> 1) stg_actors.csv
> headers: code,name,actor_type,notes
> actor_type enum: institution|agency|person|court|vendor|government|unknown
> 
> 2) stg_documents.csv
> headers: storage_path,title,file_type,phase_id,workstream,source_tags,notes
> 
> 3) stg_violations.csv
> headers: violation_code,title,summary,actor_code,phase_id,workstream,violation_type,severity,status,event_date,date_range_start,date_range_end,jurisdiction,source_storage_path
> violation_type enum: procedure|due_process|ada|fha|fcra|fdcpa|tort|accounting|evidence|credit|reputation|other
> severity enum: low|medium|high|critical
> status enum: draft|confirmed|disputed|archived
> 
> 4) stg_harms.csv
> headers: harm_code,title,narrative,harm_category,harmed_party,phase_id,workstream,start_date,end_date,is_ongoing,estimated_value,source_storage_path
> harm_category enum: housing|economic|financial|health_safety|non_economic|professional|property|credit|third_party
> harmed_party enum: self|family|partner|ally|roommate|animal|other
> 
> 5) stg_damage_entries.csv
> headers: harm_code,entry_date,category,description,amount,currency,storage_path,vendor,notes
> category enum: lodging|transport|storage|food|medical|legal|replacement|lost_income|credit_cost|other
> 
> 6) stg_credit_events.csv
> headers: event_month,bureau,score,tradeline,status,dispute_status,opportunity_lost,estimated_cost,notes,storage_path
> bureau enum: experian|equifax|transunion|unknown
> dispute_status enum: none|sent|received|verified|deleted|pending
> 
> 7) stg_links.csv
> headers: link_type,left_code_or_path,right_code_or_path,relevance_note,sort_order
> link_type enum: violation_evidence|harm_evidence|harm_violation|violation_authority
> 
> Rules:
> - All enums MUST be lowercase.
> - Dates must be ISO (YYYY-MM-DD).
> - If unknown, leave blank; do not invent.
> - Do not include UUIDs anywhere.
> - Do not output any other files.
> Begin.
> ```
> 
> This turns Gemini into a controlled extractor instead of a schema corrupter.
> 
> ---
>

> Do **Path 1** (fill_user_id trigger) + **staging ETL**. That’s the best balance of speed and stability.

> - creates `app.owner_id()`
> - creates `app.fill_user_id()`
> - adds triggers to **every table** you listed (all 20)
> - adds key uniqueness constraints for import repeatability
> 
> No guesswork, no more CSV failures.

> 
> ---
> 
> ## TL;DR (Executive Decision)
> 
> **Use Supabase MCP + Codex as your ingestion and validation layer.**  
> Gemini becomes *analysis-only*, not a writer to the database.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What MCP Actually Solves (and why this matters)
> 
> CSV import has these fatal problems:
> - No `auth.uid()` → `user_id` breaks
> - No triggers reliably firing
> - No validation feedback loop
> - Gemini produces malformed enums/headers/JSON
> - You’re debugging blind
> 
> **Supabase MCP fixes all of that**:
> - Executes *real SQL* against your project
> - Triggers fire
> - Constraints are enforced *with explanations*
> - You can upsert, normalize, and link across tables safely
> - You can introspect schema, constraints, and data live
> 
> This is the correct tool for a **case operating system**, not a toy app.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The Correct Ingestion Model (Authoritative)
> 
> ### Roles
> - **Gemini** → produces *structured staging data only*
> - **Codex + Supabase MCP** → validates, normalizes, inserts into real tables
> - **Database** → source of truth
> 
> No direct Gemini → database writes. Ever.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Step 1: Lock in Single-User Default (once, globally)
> 
> You already agreed you’re the only user. Good.
> 
> ### A. Create owner function (you already approved this idea)
> 
> ```sql
> create schema if not exists app;
> 
> create or replace function app.owner_id()
> returns uuid
> language sql
> stable
> as $$
>   select 'e7b2ecff-2e1b-4b96-9627-36f069519521'::uuid
> $$;
> ```
> 
> ### B. Universal trigger (this is the key move)
> 
> ```sql
> create or replace function app.fill_user_id()
> returns trigger
> language plpgsql
> as $$
> begin
>   if new.user_id is null then
>     new.user_id := app.owner_id();
>   end if;
>   return new;
> end;
> $$;
> ```
> 
> You will attach this to **every table with `user_id`**:
> - actors
> - documents
> - violations
> - harms
> - envelopes
> - packets
> - packet_items
> - drafts
> - damage_entries
> - credit_events
> - etc.
> 
> This instantly fixes:
> - CSV imports
> - MCP inserts
> - SQL backfills
> - future automation
> 
> I can generate the **full trigger attach script for all ~20 tables** if you want — say the word.
>

> # Step 3: Use MCP + Codex to ingest correctly
> 
> Now the important part: **Codex + MCP replaces CSV import entirely**.
> 
> ### What Codex + MCP can do that CSV cannot
> - Run `insert … select` logic
> - Upsert by business keys (`violation_code`, `harm_code`, etc.)
> - Resolve joins (`actor_code → actor_id`)
> - Enforce enums via `lower()` and `check`
> - Explain errors *before* data is written
> - Populate join tables safely
> 
> ### Example: ingest actors (pattern)
> ```sql
> insert into public.actors (code, name, actor_type, notes)
> select
>   code,
>   name,
>   lower(actor_type),
>   notes
> from stg_actors
> on conflict (user_id, code) do update
> set
>   name = excluded.name,
>   actor_type = excluded.actor_type,
>   notes = excluded.notes;
> ```
> 
> Codex can:
> - Run this
> - Show you the affected rows
> - Explain failures
> - Let you fix and re-run without damage
> 
> ---
> 
> # Step 4: How envelopes fit into this (specifically)
> 
> Envelopes are **transport artifacts**, not evidence.
> 
> Correct handling:
> - Insert envelopes via MCP SQL
> - Then create packets (`packet_type = 'efile'`)
> - Then link documents once PDFs exist in `documents`
> 
> This avoids the “half-imported envelope” problem you just hit.

### Assistant
> Yes. On Windows + Antigravity, the cleanest approach is: **install Codex CLI via npm, configure MCP in the Codex config file, then authenticate.** Two workable modes:

> - **Acceptable:** run Codex natively in PowerShell (works, but you may hit sandbox/permissions quirks). citeturn0search5

> Below are both paths.
>

>

>

> wsl --install
> ```
> 
> Reboot when it tells you to. Then open **Ubuntu** from Start Menu.
> 
> ### 2) Install Node.js in WSL
> In Ubuntu:
> 
> ```bash
> sudo apt update
> sudo apt install -y nodejs npm
> node -v
> npm -v
> ```
>

> codex --version
> ```

>

>

>

> ```

> ```
> 
> Supabase MCP setup behavior (browser login redirect) is documented. citeturn0search1
> 
> ### 6) Login / authenticate

> codex mcp login supabase
> ```
> 
> This opens a browser for approval. citeturn0search1
>

> ```

> # Phase 02 — Credit / FCRA (Print Section)
> 
> ## Purpose
> Create a court-usable, regulator-usable, and settlement-ready record showing:
> 1) inaccurate furnishing by FCFCU,
> 2) failed reinvestigations (Experian/Equifax/TransUnion),

### Assistant
> Good — this is a **classic, boring Linux permissions issue**, not you doing anything wrong. We can fix it cleanly without breaking your system.
> 
> You have **three sane options**. I’ll rank them from **best → fastest → brute force**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Option A (RECOMMENDED): Use a user-local global npm directory  
> This is the **correct, non-hacky fix**.
> 
> ### 1. Create a local npm global directory
> ```bash
> mkdir -p ~/.npm-global
> ```
> 
> ### 2. Tell npm to use it
> ```bash
> npm config set prefix '~/.npm-global'
> ```
> 
> ### 3. Add it to your PATH
> Edit your shell config (likely `.bashrc` or `.zshrc`):
> 
> ```bash
> nano ~/.bashrc
> ```
> 
> Add this line at the bottom:
> ```bash
> export PATH="$HOME/.npm-global/bin:$PATH"
> ```
> 
> Save, then reload:
> ```bash
> source ~/.bashrc
> ```
> 
> ### 4. Install Codex again
> ```bash
> npm i -g @openai/codex@latest
> ```
> 
> ### 5. Verify
> ```bash
> codex --version
> ```
> 
> ✅ This avoids `sudo`, avoids breaking system Node, and works perfectly with MCP.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Option B (FAST): Use `npx` instead of global install
> If you just want Codex **now**, no setup:
> 
> ```bash
> npx @openai/codex@latest
> ```
> 
> or
> 
> ```bash
> npx @openai/codex
> ```
> 
> This:
> - downloads Codex on demand
> - runs it once
> - requires **zero permissions**
> 
> Downside: not persistent, slightly slower each run.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Option C (NOT IDEAL): sudo install  
> I only list this so you know why **not** to do it.
> 
> ```bash
> sudo npm i -g @openai/codex@latest
> ```
> 
> This works, but:
> - can poison permissions later
> - causes pain when updating Node/npm
> - not worth it unless this is a disposable VM
> 
> ---
> 
> ## After Codex installs (next exact steps)
> Once `codex` runs, do **exactly this**:
> 
> ```bash
> codex mcp add supabase --url "https://mcp.supabase.com/mcp?project_ref=igaveicxkdqmjfxyakwb&features=docs,database,debugging,functions,storage"
> ```
> 
> Then:
> ```bash
> codex mcp login supabase
> ```
> 
> Then:
> ```bash
> codex
> ```
> 
> Inside Codex:
> ```text
> /mcp
> ```
> 
> If MCP shows Supabase connected, you’re done.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Reality check (important)
> Even **with Codex working**, Gemini auto-populating 20 relational tables was always going to be brittle. You didn’t fail — that approach is just too optimistic.
> 
> **Correct architecture going forward** (we’ll do this once Codex works):
> - Codex reads schema
> - Codex generates **controlled seed scripts**
> - You import **table by table**, not CSV soup
> - `user_id` defaulted at DB level so imports stop failing
> 
> For now, you did the right thing switching back to **printing and phase progression**. Tooling can come back once the ground truth is stable.
